(h)  No more than one liquor license shall be held by any person within the city. For the purpose of this subsection, any person owning a beneficial interest of five percent or more of any licensed establishment shall be considered a licensee. For golf courses partially within the city and partially in another municipality, the license from the other municipality shall not be considered a violation of this subsection. 
(i)  The council may issue the number of liquor licenses authorized by statute or restrict such number from time to time as it may, in its discretion, deem proper. 
(j)  No on-sale sales of liquor shall be made between the hours of 1:00 a.m. and 8:00 a.m. on any weekday, Monday through Saturday inclusive. On-sale sales of liquor shall not be permitted on Sunday, unless an on-sale Sunday liquor license is held by the licensee. Hours of Sunday sales shall be those set by Minn. Stats. § 340A.504, as it may be amended from time to time. 
(k)  For the purpose of this subsection, any person under the age of 21 years shall be considered a minor. It is unlawful for any: 
(1)  Licensee to sell liquor on any day or during any hour when sales of liquor are not permitted by law. 
(2)  Person to purchase liquor on any day or during any hour when sales of liquor are not permitted by law. 
(3)  Minor to be in or upon licensed premises, except if accompanied by a parent or guardian; and it is unlawful for the licensee to permit such unaccompanied minor to remain upon licensed premises. 
(4)  Licensee to fail, where doubt could exist, to require adequate proof of age of a person upon licensed premises. Proof of age for purchasing or consuming alcoholic beverages may be established only by one of the following: 
a.  A valid driver's license or identification card issued by the state, another state, or a province of Canada, and including the photograph and date of birth of the licensed person; 
b.  A valid military identification card issued by the United States Department of Defense; 
c.  A valid passport issued by the United States; or 
d.  In the case of a foreign national, a valid passport. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 23(B)-(D); Ord. No. 03-02; Ord. No. 17-01, § 1, 6-12-2017) 
State Law reference- Hours and days of sale, Minn. Stats. § 340A.504; sales to underage persons, Minn. Stats. § 340A.503; gambling restrictions, Minn. Stats. § 340.410, subd. 5. 
Secs. 12-68-12-92. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Licenses generally, Minn. Stats. § 340A.401 et seq. 

Sec. 12-93. - Beer license required; classes. 
(a)  Required. It is unlawful for any person to sell, keep or offer for sale beer without a license therefor issued by the city. This subsection shall not apply to sales by manufacturers to wholesalers or to sales by wholesalers to persons holding a license to sell alcoholic beverages, nor shall this subsection apply to sales to the public by persons holding a license to sell on-sale or off-sale intoxicating liquors. 
(b)  License types. Licenses to sell beer shall be limited to the following types: 
(1)  Temporary on-sale beer license. A club or charitable, religious, or nonprofit organization, duly incorporated as a nonprofit or religious corporation under the laws of the state, shall qualify for a temporary on-sale beer license, subject to the following conditions: 
a.  An application for a temporary beer license shall state the exact dates and place of proposed temporary sale. 
b.  No applicant shall qualify for a temporary beer license for more than a total of seven days in any calendar year. 
c.  The council may grant a temporary beer license on premises owned or controlled by the city, but at no time shall the council be under any obligation whatsoever to do so. 
d.  Any temporary beer license may be conditioned, qualified, or restricted as the council sees fit. 
(2)  Off-sale beer licenses. Off-sale beer licenses may be issued, which permit the sale of beer at retail, subject to the following conditions: 
a.  Beer may be sold in the original package only. 
b.  Beer may be sold for the consumption off the licensed premises only. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 22(A); Ord. No. 02-02; Ord. No. 03-09) 
State Law reference- Licenses for sale of beer or malt liquor, Minn. Stats. § 340A.403, 340A.405. 
Sec. 12-94. - Liquor license required; classes. 
(a)  Generally. It is unlawful for any person to sell, keep or offer for sale any intoxicating liquor without a license therefor from the city. This subsection shall not apply: 
(1)  To possession or handling for sale or otherwise of sacramental wine or to any representative of any religious order or for use in connection with a legitimate religious ceremony; 
(2)  To such potable liquors as are prescribed by licensed physicians and dentists for therapeutic purposes; 
(3)  To industrial alcohol and its compounds not prepared or used for beverage purposes; or 
(4)  Sales by manufacturers to wholesalers duly licensed as such by the state and to sales by wholesalers to persons holding on-sale or off-sale licenses for the sale of liquor issued by the city. 
(b)  License types. Licenses to sell intoxicating liquor shall be limited to the following types: 
(1)  On-sale liquor license. On-sale liquor licenses shall be issued only to restaurants as defined in this article. 
(2)  Off-sale liquor license. These licenses may be issued only to exclusive liquor stores as defined in this article. 
(3)  On-sale Sunday liquor license. These licenses may be issued only to persons who hold a current on-sale liquor license otherwise issued by the city. 
(4)  On-sale special event license. 
a.  The council may authorize any holder of an on-sale liquor license issued by the city or by an adjacent municipality to sell liquor at any convention, banquet, conference, meeting, or social affair conducted on the premises of any sports, convention, or cultural facility owned by the city or instrumentality thereof located within the city. The licensee must be engaged to sell liquor at such an event by the person or organization permitted to use the public facility and may sell liquor only to persons attending the event. Sales of liquor may be limited to designated areas of the public facility. All such sales shall be subject to all laws relating thereto. 
b.  The council may authorize a holder of a retail on-sale intoxicating liquor license issued by the city to dispense intoxicating liquor off premises at a community festival held within the city. The authorization shall specify the area in which the intoxicating liquor must be dispensed and consumed, and shall not be issued unless the licensee demonstrates that it has liability insurance, as prescribed by this article, to cover the event. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 23(A)) 
State Law reference- Liquor licenses, Minn. Stats. § 340A.404 et seq. 
Sec. 12-95. - Applications. 
(a)  Generally. All applications shall be made available at the office of the city clerk. Information required in an application may vary depending upon the type of business organization making application and whether the application is for the original issuance of a license or a license renewal. Prior to acceptance of the application by the city clerk, all questions asked or information required by the application shall be answered and fully provided and the application fee shall be remitted to the city clerk by the applicant. The application for a license shall provide the following information: 
(1)  For all applicants: 
a.  Whether the applicant is a natural person, corporation, partnership, or other form of organization. 
b.  The type of license the applicant seeks. 
c.  The legal description of the premises to be licensed, together with a map of the area showing dimensions, location of buildings, street access, parking facilities, and the locations of the nearest place of worship and school. 
d.  The street number where the sale of alcoholic beverages is to be conducted and the rooms where alcoholic beverages are to be sold or consumed. The applicant shall submit a floor plan of the dining rooms that shall be open to the public that shows dimensions and indicates the number of persons intended to be served in each of the rooms. 
e.  The names and addresses of all persons, other than the applicant, who have any ownership, in whole or in part, of the business to be licensed, including buildings, fixtures, furniture, and stock in trade; the nature of such ownership; the amount thereof; and terms for payment or other reimbursement. Those with an ownership shall include, but not be limited to, any lessees, lessors, mortgagees, mortgagors, lenders, lien holders, trustees, trustors and persons who have cosigned notes or otherwise loaned, pledged, or extended security for any indebtedness of the applicant. 
f.  Whether all real estate and personal property taxes that are due and payable for the premises to be licensed have been paid, and if not paid, the years and amounts that are unpaid. 
g.  The name and street address of the business, if it is to be conducted under a designation, name, or style other than the name of the applicant, and a certified copy of the certificate as required by Minn. Stats. § 333.02. 
h.  Such other information as the city may request. In the case of an application for a golf course where a portion of the course is within another municipality, a license from that municipality shall be required. 
(2)  If the applicant is a natural person: 
a.  The name, place and date of birth, and street residence address of applicant. 
b.  Whether the applicant has ever used or been known by a name other than the applicant's given name, and if so, what was such name or names and information concerning dates and places where used. 
c.  Whether the applicant is a citizen of the United States or a resident alien. 
d.  Whether the applicant is married or single. 
e.  Whether the applicant is a registered voter and, if so, where. 
f.  Street addresses at which the applicant has lived during the preceding ten years. 
g.  The type, name, and location of every business or occupation the applicant has been engaged in during the preceding ten years. 
h.  Names and addresses of the applicant's employers and partners, if any, for the preceding ten years. 
i.  Whether the applicant, or a parent, brother, sister, or child of the applicant, has ever been convicted of any felony, crime, or violation of any ordinance other than traffic. If so, the applicant shall furnish information as to the time and place of such conviction and the related offense. 
j.  Whether the applicant, or a parent, brother, sister or child of the applicant, has ever been engaged in the operation of a saloon, hotel, restaurant, cafe, tavern or other business that served alcoholic beverages. If so, the applicant shall furnish information as to the time, place and length of time of the involvement in such establishment. 
k.  Whether the applicant has ever been in military service. If so, the applicant shall, upon request, provide evidence of all discharges. 
l.  The name, address and business address of each individual who is engaged in the state in the business of selling, manufacturing or distributing alcoholic beverages and who is nearer of kin to the applicant than second cousin, whether of whole or half blood, computed by the rules of civil law, or who is a brother-in-law or sister-in-law of the applicant. 
(3)  If the applicant is a partnership, the names and addresses of all general and limited partners and all information concerning each general partner as is required in subsection (a)(2) of this section. The managing partners shall be designated, and the interest of each general and limited partner in the business shall be disclosed. A true copy of the partnership agreement shall be submitted with the application, and if the partnership is required to file a certificate as to a trade name under Minn. Stats. § 333.02, a certified copy of such certificate shall be submitted. The license shall be issued in the name of the partnership. 
(4)  If the applicant is a corporation or other organization: 
a.  The name of the organization and the state of organization. 
b.  A true copy of the certificate of incorporation or, if a foreign corporation, a certificate of authority as described in Minn. Stats. § 303.03. 
c.  The name of the general manager, food/beverage manager, four principal corporate officers, proprietor and other persons in charge of the premises to be licensed and all the information about said persons as is required in subsection (a)(2) of this section. 
d.  A list of all persons who, together with their spouse, parent, brother, sister, or child, own or control an interest as defined herein in the corporation or organization to be licensed, together with their addresses and all the information regarding such persons as is required in subsection (a)(2) of this section. 
(5)  If the applicant is a club: 
a.  The name of the club, and, where appropriate, the name of the establishment serving the club. 
b.  The date that the club was first incorporated, and, where appropriate, the date that the establishment serving the club was incorporated or otherwise established. True copies of the articles of incorporation, bylaws, or other similar governing documents shall be submitted with the application. 
c.  The date that the club was first organized and the place of such organization. 
d.  A sworn statement that the club has been in existence for at least three years. The statement shall be made by a person who has personal knowledge of the facts stated therein. In the event that no person can make such a statement, satisfactory documentary proof may be submitted in support of such facts. 
e.  The number of members of the club. 
f.  The name of the general manager, proprietor, food/beverage manager, corporate officers, and other information regarding such persons as is required in subsection (a)(2) of this section. 
(b)  False statements. It is unlawful for any applicant to intentionally make a false statement or omission upon any application. Any false statement in such application or any willful omission to state any information called for on such application shall, upon discovery of such falsehood or omission, result in an automatic denial of the application or, if a license has already issued, shall render any such license void and of no effect. 
(c)  Application fee. At the time of submitting an application, the applicant shall pay a non-refundable application fee to cover the costs of the city in processing the application and investigating the facts contained therein. 
(d)  Renewal. Applications for renewal of all licenses under this division shall be made at least 60 days prior to the date of expiration of the current license and shall contain such information as is required by the city clerk. This time requirement may be waived by the council for good and sufficient cause. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subds. 2-4, 10; Ord. No. 03-02) 
Sec. 12-96. - Persons disqualified. 
(a)  No retail license may be issued to: 
(1)  A person under 21 years of age; 
(2)  A person who has had an intoxicating liquor or 3.2 percent malt liquor license revoked within five years of the license application, or to any person who, at the time of the violation, owns any interest, whether as a holder of more than five percent of the capital stock of a corporation licensee, as a partner or otherwise, in the premises or in the business conducted thereon, or to a corporation, partnership, association, enterprise, business or firm in which any such person is in any manner interested; 
(3)  A person not of good moral character and repute; or 
(4)  A person who has a direct or indirect interest in a manufacturer, brewer, or wholesaler. 
(b)  In addition, no new retail license shall be issued to, and there shall be no license renewal of the license of, a person who, within five years of the license application, has been convicted of a felony or a willful violation of a federal or state law or local ordinance governing the manufacture, sale, distribution, or possession for sale or distribution of an alcoholic beverage. The city council o may require that fingerprints be taken and forwarded to the Federal Bureau of Investigation for purposes of a criminal history check. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 9) 
State Law reference- General eligibility requirements for alcoholic beverage licenses, Minn. Stats. § 340A.402. 
Sec. 12-97. - Manager or resident agent. 
(a)  Before a license is issued under this division to an individual who is a nonresident of the city, or more than one individual whether or not they are residents of the city, or to a corporation, partnership, or association, the applicant or applicants shall appoint in writing a natural person who is its manager or agent. Such manager or agent shall, by the terms of his written consent: 
(1)  Take full responsibility for the sale of any alcoholic beverages at the licensed premises; and 
(2)  Serve as agent for service of notices and other processes relating to the license. 
(b)  Such manager or agent must be a person who, by reason of age, character, reputation, and other attributes, could qualify individually as a licensee. If such manager or agent ceases to act in such capacity for the licensee without appointment of a successor, the license shall be subject to revocation or suspension. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 8) 
Sec. 12-98. - Delinquent taxes and charges. 
    No license shall be issued under this division for any premises upon which property taxes, assessments, or installments thereof or other financial claims of the city (or in the case of a golf course partially in another municipality, the foregoing obligations to that municipality) are owed by the applicant and are delinquent and unpaid. For the purpose of this section, the term "applicant" includes persons and related persons owning, directly or indirectly, at least a 50-percent interest in the proposed license premises or in the entity making the application. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 11; Ord. No. 03-02) 
Sec. 12-99. - Issuance. 
(a)  Public hearing. The city council shall conduct a hearing on the application within a reasonable period following receipt by the city clerk of a complete and accurate application. At least ten days in advance of the city council hearing on an application, the city clerk shall cause notice of the hearing to be published in the official newspaper of the city, setting forth the day, time, and place of the hearing; the name of the applicant; the licensed premises where the sale of alcoholic beverages is to be conducted; and the type of license which is sought. At the hearing, opportunity shall be given to any person to be heard for or against the granting of the license. Additional hearings on the application may be held if the city council deems additional hearings necessary. After the hearing or hearings on the Application, the city council may, in its discretion, grant or deny the application. 
(b)  Issuance; license fee. The council may approve the issuance of a license pursuant to this division for the period of the remainder of the then-current license year or for the entire ensuing license year. Upon such approval, the city clerk shall prepare the license in the form prescribed by the council. Prior to issuing a license, the applicant shall pay to the city clerk the necessary license fee. For licenses that are to become effective other than on the first day of the license year, the fee to be paid as a condition to issuance shall be a pro rata share of the annual license fee. Licenses shall be valid only at one location and on the licensed premises therein described. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 5(A),(B)) 
Sec. 12-100. - Fixing license and application fees. 
    All fees provided for in this article, including application fees and license fees, shall be fixed and determined by resolution of the council. Such fees may, from time to time, be amended by the council by resolution. A copy of the resolution shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk and shall be available for inspection during regular business hours of the city. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 20) 
State Law reference- Retail license fees, Minn. Stats. § 340A.408. 
Sec. 12-101. - Denial or termination. 
    The council shall refuse to issue or renew a license upon a finding that it is not in the public interest to issue or renew the license, or if the person to whom the license is to be issued or renewed if or the location for which the license is to be issued or renewed is ineligible for such license under state law. Licenses shall terminate only by expiration or revocation. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 5(E)) 
Sec. 12-102. - Licensed premises. 
    A license issued under the provisions of this division shall be valid only for the licensed premises specified therein, and all transactions relating to a sale of alcoholic beverages under such license must take place within the area specified as the licensed premises. No person shall consume alcoholic beverages on the licensed premises that are not sold by the licensee of the premises. Prior to issuance or renewal of a license, the licensed premises and the property on which the premises is situated shall be inspected and found to be in conformity with the requirements of this Code, the state building code, and the state fire code. In the case of a golf course partially within another municipality, with both a city license and a license issued by that municipality, alcoholic beverages may be sold in the other municipality and consumed in the city so long as the consumption and sale comply with both licenses. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 14; Ord. No. 03-02) 
State Law reference- Retail alcoholic beverage license to be issued only for a space that is compact and contiguous, Minn. Stats. § 340A.410, subd. 7. 
Sec. 12-103. - Financial responsibility of licensees. 
(a)  Proof. No beer or liquor license shall be issued, maintained, or renewed unless and until the applicant has provided proof of financial responsibility with regard to liability imposed by Minn. Stats. § 340A.801 by filing with the city: 
(1)  A certificate that there is in effect an insurance policy issued by an insurer required to be licensed under Minn. Stats. § 60A.07, subd. 4, or by an insurer recognized as an eligible surplus lines carrier pursuant to Minn. Stats. § 60A.206 or pool providing minimum coverages of: 
a.  $100,000.00 because of bodily injury to any one person in any one occurrence, and $300,000.00 because of bodily injury to two or more persons in any one occurrence, and in the amount of $100,000.00 because of injury to or destruction of property of others in any one occurrence; and 
b.  $100,000.00 for loss of means of support of any one person in any one occurrence, and, subject to the limit of one person, $300,000.00 for loss of means of support of two or more persons in any one occurrence (an annual aggregate policy limit for dram shop liability of not less than $300,000.00 per policy may be included in the policy provision); or 
(2)  A bond of a surety company with minimum coverages as provided in subsection (a)(1) of this section. 
(b)  City named as additional insured. The insurer or surety shall name the city as an additional insured or covered party under the insurance policy or bonds provided in accordance with this section. 
(c)  Notice of cancellation. A liability insurance policy required by this section must provide that it may not be canceled for: 
(1)  Any cause, except for nonpayment of premium, by either the insured or the insurer unless the canceling party has first given 60 days' notice in writing to the insured of intent to cancel the policy; and 
(2)  Nonpayment of premium unless the canceling party has first given ten days' notice in writing to the insured of intent to cancel the policy. 
In the event of a policy cancellation, the insurer will send notice to the city clerk at the same time that a cancellation request is received from or a notice is sent to the insured. 
(d)  Renewal. Every application for the issuance or renewal of a license must include a copy of each summons received by the applicant under Minn. Stats. § 340A.802 during the preceding year. 
(e)  Documents submitted to commissioner. All proofs of financial responsibility and exemption affidavits filed with the city under this section will be submitted by the city to the state commissioner of public safety. 
(f)  Exemptions. Subsection (a) of this section does not apply to licenses to be issued to licensees who by affidavit establish that: 
(1)  They are on-sale 3.2 percent malt liquor licensees with sales of less than $25,000.00 of 3.2 percent malt liquor for the preceding year; 
(2)  They are off-sale 3.2 percent malt liquor licensees with sales of less than $50,000.00 of 3.2 percent malt liquor for the preceding year; 
(3)  They are holders of on-sale wine licenses with sales of less than $25,000.00 for wine for the preceding year; or 
(4)  They are holders of temporary wine licenses issued under law. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 21) 
State Law reference- Insurance requirements, Minn. Stats. § 340A.409. 
Sec. 12-104. - Special conditions. 
    Notwithstanding any provision of law to the contrary, the council may, upon a finding of the necessity therefor, place such special conditions and restrictions, in addition to those stated in this division, upon any license as it, in its discretion, may deem reasonable and justified. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 13) 
Sec. 12-105. - Transfer. 
    No license may be sold, assigned, or otherwise transferred to another person or location without the written approval of the council. The council shall not approve the transfer upon a finding that the transfer is not in the public interest or if the person to whom the transfer is to be made or the location to which the license is to be transferred is ineligible for such license under state law. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 5(D)) 
Sec. 12-106. - Duplicate licenses. 
    Duplicates of all original licenses under this division may be issued by the city clerk without action by the council upon licensee's sworn affidavit that the original has been lost and upon payment of a fee, as provided in the schedule of city fees adopted by the city council from time to time. All duplicate licenses shall be clearly marked "DUPLICATE." 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 6) 
Sec. 12-107. - Posting. 
    All licensees shall conspicuously post their licenses in the premises for which they are issued. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 7) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Minn. Stats. § 340A.410, subd. 4. 
Sec. 12-108. - Revocation, suspension, or other discipline of licensee. 
(a)  Upon a finding that the licensee has: 
(1)  Sold alcoholic beverages to another retail licensee for the purpose of resale; 
(2)  Purchased alcoholic beverages from another retail licensee for the purpose of resale; 
(3)  Conducted or permitted the conduct of gambling on the licensed premises in violation of the law; 
(4)  Failed to remove or dispose of alcoholic beverages when ordered by the commissioner to do so under Minn. Stats. § 340A.508, subd. 3; or 
(5)  Failed to comply with an applicable statute, rule, or ordinance relating to alcoholic beverages, the council may: 
a.  Suspend the license for a period not to exceed 60 days; 
b.  Revoke the license; 
c.  Impose a civil fine on the licensee not to exceed $2,000.00 for each violation; or 
d.  Impose any combination of the foregoing sanctions. 
(b)  No suspension, fine, or revocation shall take effect until the licensee has been afforded an opportunity for a hearing before the council, a committee of the council, or a hearing examiner, as may be determined by the council in an action calling the hearing. Such hearing shall be called by the council upon written notice to the licensee, served in person or by certified mail not less than ten nor more than 30 days prior to the hearing date, stating the time, place, and purpose thereof. The hearing shall comply with Minn. Stats. §§ 14.57-14.69. This section does not require the city to conduct the hearing before an employee of the state office of administrative hearings. 
(c)  The council shall revoke a license upon conviction of any licensee or agent or employee of a licensee for willfully violating any law relating to the sale or possession of alcoholic beverages. If it shall be made to appear at the hearing thereon that such violation was not willful, the council may order suspension or a fine not to exceed $2,000.00, provided that revocation shall be ordered upon the third such violation or offense. The following shall also be grounds for such actions by the city: 
(1)  That the licensee suffered or permitted illegal acts upon the licensed premises unrelated to the sale of alcoholic beverages; 
(2)  That the licensee had knowledge of such illegal acts upon the licensed premises, but failed to report the same to police; 
(3)  That the licensee failed or refused to cooperate fully with police in investigating such alleged illegal acts upon licensed premises; or 
(4)  That the licensee failed to maintain financial responsibility required by this article. 
(Prior Code, ch. 402, subd. 5(F)) 
State Law reference- License revocation or suspension, Minn. Stats. § 340A.415. 
Secs. 12-109-12-129. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - BINGO AND OTHER LAWFUL GAMBLING[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Lawful gambling, Minn. Stats. ch. 349; local regulation of lawful gambling, Minn. Stats. § 349.213. 

Sec. 12-130. - Bingo. 
(a)  State regulations adopted. The regulatory provisions of Minn. Stats. §§ 349.11-349.23, which regulate the conduct of bingo games in the state, are hereby adopted by the city. 
(b)  Licenses. An organization wishing to conduct a game of bingo in the city must obtain a license. All licenses shall be obtained from the city clerk only after approval by the city council. Application for licenses shall be filed with the clerk on the forms furnished by the state. The fee for the license shall be annually established by the city council. 
(c)  Review of application. No license shall be issued until the application has been referred to the building inspector, the fire department and the police department for review. 
(d)  Suspension or revocation of license. The city council shall have the power to suspend or revoke the license issued to any organization for violations of any of the regulations or terms of this article. The organization shall be given 20 days' notice and shall be granted an opportunity to be heard before such action is taken. 
(e)  License expiration. All licenses shall expire on December 31 following the date of issuance, unless sooner revoked or suspended for violation of the terms of this article. If a license granted hereunder is not renewed previous to its expiration, then all rights granted by such license shall cease. 
(f)  Exemption. An organization qualifying for exemption pursuant to Minn. Stats. § 349.19 shall apply directly to the city council for such exemption. The city council may, by motion, grant an organization so qualifying permission to conduct the game of bingo. 
(Prior Code, ch. 403; Ord. No. 04-03) 
Sec. 12-131. - Gambling licenses. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. 
    Private gambling includes pull-tabs and other games of chance where entries are sold, the game may be played, and prize payments are made, all on the same premises. Private gambling does not include games or contests administered on a state-wide basis, such as state lotteries, nor does it include bingo, which is licensed under section 12-130. 
    Trade area consists of the City of Oak Grove and the Cities of Andover, Anoka, Ham Lake, East Bethel, Bethel, St. Francis, and Nowthen. 
    Temporary gambling license means a license issued pursuant to an application for exempt status, to last for a period of less than six days. 
(b)  State regulations adopted. The regulatory provisions of Minn. Stats. §§ 349.11-349.23 are hereby adopted in the city, with the addition of the provisions of this article. Where the provisions of this article differ from the state statute, the provisions of this article shall control. 
(c)  Local authority. The state gambling control board licenses gambling operations within the state. As part of this licensing, the gambling control board requests that the city either approve or deny applications for any gambling operation located within the city. The city adopts the following measures to guide city approval of private gambling operations, in addition to the requirements imposed by state law: 
(1)  It is a violation of this section to gamble or to operate gambling operations without city approval of a state gambling license. 
(2)  By resolution, the city may restrict the number or frequency of temporary gambling license approvals if the city finds that events held with temporary gambling licenses are detracting from the general welfare of the city or creating a nuisance. A maximum of three non-temporary gambling license approvals shall be issued to organizations in any year, to allow gambling at a maximum of five total locations for the year. 
(3)  A licensed organization conducting private gambling within the jurisdiction of the city shall expend all of its expenditures for lawful purposes on local purposes conducted or located within the trade area of the city. 
(4)  A licensed organization conducting private gambling within the jurisdiction of the city shall contribute ten percent of its net profits derived from lawful gambling conducted at premises within the city's jurisdiction to a fund administered and regulated by the city without cost to the fund, for disbursement by the city for lawful purposes. 
(Prior Code, ch. 405; Ord. No. 99-1; Ord. No. 18-09, § 1, 10-8-2018) 
Secs. 12-132-12-160. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - FIELD PARTIES AND LARGE ASSEMBLIES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-161. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Field party is defined as a gathering or projected gathering of more than 50 but less than 3,500 people, held partially or completely out of doors, on public or private property, and at which intoxicating beverages, beer or other intoxicating chemicals are used or dispensed by any participant, whether or not a fee is collected from the participant. For the purposes of this article, field parties do not include family gatherings or weddings held on the premises of a private residence. 
(Prior Code, ch. 404, subd. 1; Ord. No. 98-05) 
Secs. 12-162-12-188. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

Sec. 12-189. - Required; term. 
(a)  No person shall permit, maintain, promote, conduct, advertise, participate in, be present at, act as entrepreneur, undertake, organize, manage, or sell or give tickets to a field party held in any area of the city, whether on public or private property, unless a license to hold the field party has first been issued by the city clerk. Application for a license must be made at least 45 days in advance of the date that the field party will be held. A police officer, upon discovering a field party that is unlicensed or upon declaring any license to be void, shall order the persons present to disperse, and it shall be unlawful for any person to continue to be present at the field party. 
(b)  No field party license shall be valid for more than a 48-hour period, beginning with the applicant's start time as stated on the permit application. 
(Prior Code, ch. 404, subd. 2; Ord. No. 98-05) 
Sec. 12-190. - Application; fee. 
(a)  Forms. Application shall be made to the city clerk on forms to be supplied by the city and shall contain the following information: 
(1)  The name, address and telephone number of the applicant. 
(2)  The precise location of the proposed field party, including the north, south, east, and west boundaries, the date and specific times during which the field party will be in progress, the dates and times of expected musical or other performances that will be a source of significant noise, the expected number of guests, and the maximum number of tickets to be printed, if the event uses tickets. 
(3)  A written acknowledgment of consent to hold a field party by the owner of the property upon which the field party and any parking by participants of the field party will occur. 
(4)  A statement as to whether or not intoxicating beverages, beer or other intoxicating chemicals will be furnished, and if so, whether a fee of any kind will be sought or collected, or whether voluntary contributions will be sought or collected. If a fee of any kind will be sought or collected or if voluntary contributions will be sought or collected, the applicant shall comply with the provisions of section 12-94. Regardless of whether or not a fee will be sought or collected, the applicant shall furnish a statement detailing the persons by name or specific class of persons authorized to sell or distribute intoxicating beverages, beer, or other intoxicating chemicals. 
(5)  Unless waived or modified by the city council for good cause, a written statement demonstrating that the applicant has adequate measures to protect the health and safety of participants, including, but not limited to, the following: 
a.  The means by which the field party will be illuminated. 
b.  The means by which emergency vehicles may be summoned, the means of access of emergency vehicles to the field party site, and the provisions for on-site first aid to be present at the field party site. 
c.  Adequate space for the number of expected guests and provision for both space and, if the city council finds that significant aesthetic or environmental damage may occur if parking is allowed off paved surfaces, sufficient paved surface to park the vehicles of expected guests. Sufficient paved surface shall be deemed to exist if there is one parking space for every four persons, calculated using the maximum expected attendees. 
d.  Proof that the applicant possesses a certificate of liability insurance coverage in at least the sum of $100,000.00 for injury to any one person, $300,000.00 for injury to more than one person, and $25,000.00 for property damage, naming the city as an additional insured party during the license period. 
e.  The means by which potable water, meeting all federal and state requirements for sanitary quality and at the rate of at least one gallon per person per day, will be made available for expected attendees. 
f.  The means by which enclosed toilets, separate for men and women, conveniently located throughout the site and sufficient to provide facilities, in accord with state board of health regulations, for the maximum number of attendees expected will be made available, including plans for keeping the toilets clean, operable, and free of refuse. 
g.  The means by which state-licensed private security officers and/or public police service will be provided for the maximum numbers of attendees on and near the site to adequately control the attendees as well as traffic, property damage, and other disruptions to public health and safety. 
h.  A statement of the last ten events, or events in the last three years held, put on, or promoted by the applicant, including copies of the applicable license or permit under which the events were conducted, and the mailing address and telephone number of the city, municipality, county, town, or other government unit having jurisdiction over the event site. 
i.  The means by which solid waste will be collected and disposed of from the site, sufficient to dispose of at least 2.5 pounds of solid waste per person per day. 
j.  The means by which the site will be enclosed to prevent people in excess of the maximum number of attendees from gaining access to the grounds, such as a wall or fence of sufficient size and strength. 
k.  A statement that all public accommodations on the site, including food, drinking water, and restroom facilities, are accessible, to the extent required by state and federal law for such accommodations, to persons with disabilities. 
(b)  Fees. All applications for field party licenses shall be accompanied by a fee that shall be determined by the city council. In addition to the license fee, the council may fix an investigation fee commensurate with the costs of an investigation sufficient to ensure the validity of the application statements and the adequacy of measures to protect public health and safety. 
(Prior Code, ch. 404, subd. 3; Ord. No. 98-05) 
Sec. 12-191. - Issuance. 
(a)  Issuance criteria. The city clerk shall have the authority to issue or deny licenses for field parties projected to have less than 500 attendees, but may refer the decision directly to the city council. The city clerk shall issue the license if all of the provisions of this section have been satisfied. The council shall issue all licenses for field parties projected to have 500 or more attendees, provided that, for all field parties regardless of size, with regard to section 12-190(a)(5), the measures below shall be deemed insufficient measures to protect the safety of participants: 
(1)  Illumination primarily from motor vehicle headlights, ground fires, or other light sources located less than ten feet above ground; 
(2)  The lack of a reliable communication device located within 1,000 feet of the proposed site. A stationary conventional (using wires) telephone is deemed a reliable communication device. A common citizen's band radio shall not be deemed a reliable communication device. A cellular or other wireless telephone, including a car phone, shall not be deemed a reliable communication device. Other means of communication will be deemed reliable communication devices by decision, after consideration, of the council. 
(3)  The lack of an inclement weather monitoring and storm signaling system capable of alerting attendees of weather hazards in sufficient time for attendees to disperse or seek shelter, and sufficient for the applicant to render safe equipment which may constitute a hazard in inclement weather. 
(4)  The existence of the site at a location greater than 1,000 feet from any traveled public road, or the existence of access to a traveled public road where the access is not marked by reflectorized markings, or not passable by a four-wheeled, two-wheel drive emergency motor vehicle, or not of sufficient width to accommodate the passage of emergency vehicles. 
And further provided that, for all field parties regardless of size, reasonable investigation into the prior events held, put on, or promoted by the applicant provide a basis for believing that the applicant's facility and security measures will be reasonably adequate to provide access to persons with disabilities, and to prevent personal injury, property or environmental damage, breaches of the peace, and event-related crime. 
(b)  Review by city council. If the clerk denies a license, or, for field parties projected to have 500 or more attendees, refers the decision directly to the city council, the applicant shall have the right to have the application reviewed by the city council by placement on the agenda of the next regular city council meeting. 
(c)  Report to sheriff. If a license is issued, a copy thereof shall be forwarded to the office of the county sheriff by the city. 
(d)  Conditions of license. All licenses issued pursuant to this article shall clearly state the dates and times during which the license is valid, and any peace officer shall have the right to order the participants to disperse should the activity extend beyond the time limitation set out on the face of the license. Any license issued shall be subject to the following conditions, which shall be printed on the face of the license, and shall read as follows: 
This license shall be rendered void if any of the following conditions are found to exist at the field party site: a. The commission of the crime of assault, disorderly conduct, or breach of the peace by any participant on or near the field party site. b. The consumption or possession, on or near the field party site, of any intoxicating beverage or beer by any person prohibited from engaging in said consumption or possession by Minn. Stats. ch. 340A. c. The sale or distribution of intoxicating beverages or beer by any person or in any manner inconsistent with the applicant's application for a field party license statement pursuant to section 12-190(a)(4). d. The failure of an applicant to be physically present within the boundaries of the field party site during the entire duration of the field party. e. The maintenance of any nuisance or other violation under any city ordinance. f. The consumption or possession, on or near the field party site, by a field party attendee, of any intoxicant, including, but not limited to, prescription or non-prescription medications used in a manner inconsistent with their labeling, inhalants, hallucinogens, or narcotics, in violation of Minnesota or federal law. Upon observing the violation of any of the conditions of a license, a peace officer shall declare the license to be void, and shall order the participants to disperse.  
(Prior Code, ch. 404, subd. 4; Ord. No. 98-05) 
Secs. 12-192-12-220. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - FIREWORKS[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- Fireworks, Minn. Stats. § 624.40 et seq. 

Sec. 12-221. - Definition. 
    The term "fireworks" is defined by Minn. Stats. § 624.20, a copy of which is available at city hall. 
(Prior Code, ch. 407, subd. 3; Ord. No. 06-04) 
Sec. 12-222. - State regulations adopted. 
    Minn. Stats. §§ 624.20-624.25, which regulate the sale, possession and use of fireworks in Minnesota, are hereby adopted. 
(Prior Code, ch. 407, subd. 2; Ord. No. 06-04) 
Sec. 12-223. - License required for sale. 
(a)  No person shall sell any fireworks without first obtaining a license. All licenses shall be obtained from the city clerk only after approval from the fire chief or his designee with final approval by city council. Final approval or denial shall be given within 30 days upon finding the application is complete. The fee for the license shall be annually established by the city council, which is limited by Minn. Stats. § 624.20. 
(b)  Prior to issuing the fireworks sale license, the fire chief and/or his designee will inspect the proposed location for selling fireworks. An application for a fireworks sale license must include: 
(1)  A letter from the property owner granting permission to the applicant to sell and/or store fireworks on the property; 
(2)  A floor plan designating the area where the fireworks will be sold and/or stored; 
(3)  A list of the fireworks that will be sold. (The list must include the name, weight, quantity and material safety data sheets); 
(4)  A certificate of liability insurance coverage; 
(5)  Verification that the display of fireworks for permanent or temporary retail sale complies with National Fire Protection Association Standard 1124 as referenced in Minn. Stats. § 624.20, a copy of which is available at city hall; and 
(6)  Evidence of compliance with any other necessary license or permit regulations, including statutory requirements under Minn. Stats. §§ 624.20-624.25. 
(Prior Code, ch. 407, subd. 4; Ord. No. 06-01; Ord. No. 06-04) 
Sec. 12-224. - Permit expiration. 
    All licenses shall expire on December 31 following the date of issuance, unless sooner revoked or suspended for violation of the terms of this article. 
(Prior Code, ch. 407, subds. 4, 7; Ord. No. 06-01; Ord. No. 06-04) 
Sec. 12-225. - Requirements for fireworks display license. 
    An application for a fireworks display permit must include: 
(1)  A letter from the property owner granting permission to the applicant to display fireworks on the property; 
(2)  A certificate of liability insurance coverage meeting the requirements of section 2-110; 
(3)  An application narrative verifying and illustrating compliance with Minn. Stats. § 624.22, a copy of which is available at city hall; and 
(4)  Compliance with any other necessary license or permit regulations, including statutory requirements under Minn. Stats. §§ 624.20-624.25. 
(Prior Code, ch. 407, subd. 6; Ord. No. 06-04) 
Secs. 12-226-12-243. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - SOLID WASTE COLLECTORS[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
State Law reference- Local licensing of solid waste collectors, Minn. Stats. § 115A.93; solid waste collection required, Minn. Stats. § 115.941. 

Sec. 12-244. - Garbage, recyclables and refuse; definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Compost means yard waste and other biodegradable matter that, under proper conditions, will be converted to a soil-like substance used as a soil. 
    Enforcement officials means the city administrator, or his authorized representatives, responsible for the enforcement of the provisions of this article. 
    Garbage means animal and vegetable waste resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking, and consumption of food. 
    Recyclable includes newsprint, corrugated cardboard and office paper, plastics, tin cans, aluminum, used motor oil, glass and other metal goods and other items identified as reusable or re-processable materials. 
    Refuse includes garbage and rubbish. 
    Rubbish means all inorganic solid wastes, such as ashes and other non-reusable waste. 
    Yard waste means the garden waste, leaves, lawn cuttings, weeds, and prunings generated at residential, commercial and industrial properties. 
(Prior Code, ch. 607, subd. 2) 
Sec. 12-245. - Refuse collectors. 
(a)  License required. It is unlawful to collect, haul or convey refuse from any premises in the city, other than from one's own residence, without a valid license therefor. Each such vehicle so used, except for personal disposal, must also be licensed for such activity. 
(b)  Application for license. The applicant for a collector's license or renewal of such license shall provide the following: 
(1)  The name and address of the owner of the collection service who is to be the licensee; 
(2)  A schedule of services to be made to the customer, including, but not limited to, proposed days of collection and the areas of the city within which those days of collection shall occur; 
(3)  A schedule of varying rates based on the volume or weight of the refuse collected that shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk, indicating the charge for each size container; or other schedule of charges to be applied by the licensee (The city may designate the number of categories in regard to the size of the containers); 
(4)  The frequency of service to be rendered; 
(5)  The place to which the refuse is to be hauled; 
(6)  Proof of insurance as required in subsection (d) of this section; 
(7)  Any other information the city deems necessary; and 
(8)  License fee according to the fee schedule adopted by the city council. 
(c)  Processing application. Applications for a license hereunder shall be submitted to the city for review and consideration. If the council is satisfied that the public need, convenience and good order will be served thereby, it may grant a license to such applicant. 
(d)  Insurance requirements. No license shall be issued until the applicant files with the city a current copy of the policy of public liability insurance that complies with the provisions of section 2-110. 
(e)  Term of license; license fee. Licenses shall be issued for a period of one year, expiring on December 31 of each year. The license fee shall be as established by ordinance and may be adjusted. 
(f)  Suspension or revocation of license. Any license issued hereunder may be revoked or suspended by the city council if false statements have been made in the application therefor or upon failure of a licensee to comply with any state law or local ordinance. 
(Prior Code, ch. 607, subd. 6) 
Sec. 12-246. - Refuse and recyclable collection requirements. 
(a)  Refuse collection required. Each licensee shall provide weekly collection and removal of refuse from its customers' premises in the city which normally results from day to day use of the property, except furnishings, appliances, construction waste and similar bulky waste, for which individuals shall make special collection arrangements. 
(b)  Curbside recycling. Each licensee shall provide curbside recycling to each of its customers within the city at least once every two weeks. Recyclables to be collected shall consist of at least four broad types (plastic bottles, glass bottles, metal cans and newspaper). The licensee shall also provide to the city, by July 10 and January 10 of each year, a report on the tonnage of recyclable materials collected. 
(c)  Neat and orderly collections. 
(1)  The licensee shall ensure that reasonable care in transferring the contents of the containers to his vehicle is used to avoid spillage. If any spillage occurs, the licensee, or his employee then performing the collection services, shall clean it immediately and completely. 
(2)  Vehicles shall be equipped with brooms and shovels for cleaning any spills associated with collecting or hauling garbage, recyclables or refuse. 
(3)  Collection shall be conducted in such a manner as to not create a nuisance. 
(4)  Upon each collection, the containers shall be completely emptied and replaced with lids in place. 
(d)  Tonnage reports. All haulers should report to the city on a quarterly basis the total tonnage of recyclables collected in the city. 
(e)  Collection vehicles. Vehicles used by the licensee to collect or transport garbage, refuse, or recyclables over any city street shall be properly maintained and operated and have a fully enclosed metal body capable of completely containing the contents so as to prevent offensive odors escaping therefrom and solids or liquids from leaking, spilling, dropping, or blowing from the vehicle. 
(Prior Code, ch. 607, subd. 7) 
State Law reference- Vehicle loads, Minn. Stats. § 169.81, subd. 5. 
Secs. 12-247-12-270. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - TOBACCO DEALERS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 12-271. - Definitions and interpretations. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Compliance checks means the system the city uses to investigate and ensure that those authorized to sell tobacco, tobacco products, and tobacco-related devices are following and complying with the requirements of this article. Compliance checks shall involve the use of minors as authorized by this article. Compliance checks shall also mean the use of minors who attempt to purchase tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices for educational, research and training purposes as authorized by state and federal laws. Compliance checks may also be conducted by other units of government for the purpose of enforcing appropriate federal, state, or local laws and regulations relating to tobacco, tobacco products, and tobacco-related devices. 
    Individually packaged means the practice of selling any tobacco or tobacco product wrapped individually for sale. Individually wrapped tobacco and tobacco products shall include, but not be limited to, single cigarette packs, single bags or cans of loose tobacco in any form, and single cans or other packaging of snuff or chewing tobacco. Cartons or other packaging containing more than a single pack or other container as described in this article shall not be considered individually packaged. 
    Loosie is the common term used to refer to a single or individually packaged cigarette. 
    Minor means any natural person who has not yet reached the age of 18 years. 
    Moveable place of business means any form of business operated out of a truck, van, automobile, or other type of vehicle or transportable shelter and not a fixed address store front or other permanent type of structure authorized for sales transactions. 
    Retail establishment means any place of business where tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices are available for sale to the general public. Retail establishments shall include, but not be limited to, grocery stores, convenience stores, and restaurants. 
    Sale means any transfer of goods for money, trade, barter, or other consideration. 
    Self-service merchandising means open displays of tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices in any manner where any person shall have access to the tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices without the assistance or intervention of the licensee or the licensee's employee. The assistance or intervention shall entail the actual physical exchange of the tobacco, tobacco product, or tobacco-related device between the customer and the licensee or employee. Self-service merchandising shall not include vending machines. 
    Tobacco or tobacco products means cigarettes and any product containing, made, or derived from tobacco that is intended for human consumption, whether chewed, smoked, absorbed, dissolved, inhaled, snorted, sniffed, or ingested by any other means, or any component, part, or accessory of a tobacco product; cigars; cheroots; stogies; perique; granulated, plug cut, crimp cut, ready rubbed, and other smoking tobacco; snuff; snuff flour; cavendish; plug and twist tobacco; fine cut and other chewing tobaccos; shorts; refuse scraps, clippings, cuttings and sweepings of tobacco; and other kinds and forms of tobacco. The term "tobacco" excludes any tobacco product that has been approved by the United States Food and Drug Administration for sale as a tobacco cessation product, as a tobacco dependence product, or for other medical purposes, and is being marketed and sold solely for such an approved purpose. 
    Tobacco-related devices means cigarette papers or pipes for smoking. 
    Vending machine means any mechanical, electric, electronic, or other type of device that dispenses tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices upon the insertion of money, tokens, or other forms of payment directly into the machine by the person seeking to purchase the tobacco, tobacco product, or tobacco-related device. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 2; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-272. - Penalties. 
(a)  Licensees. Any licensee found to have violated this article, or whose employee shall have violated this article, shall be charged an administrative fine of $75.00 for a first violation of this article; $200.00 for a second offense at the same licensed premises within a 24-month period; and $250.00 for a third or subsequent offense at the same location within a 24-month period. In addition, after the third offense, the license shall be suspended for not less than seven days. 
(b)  Other individuals. Other individuals, other than minors, found to be in violation of this article shall be charged an administrative fine of $100.00. 
(c)  Misdemeanor. Nothing in this section shall prohibit the city from seeking prosecution as a misdemeanor for any violation of this article. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 13; Ord. No. 97-06) 
State Law reference- Authorized penalties, Minn. Stats. § 461.13, subds. 2, 3. 
Sec. 12-273. - Violations. 
(a)  Notice. Upon discovery of a suspected violation, the alleged violator shall be issued, either personally or by mail, a citation that sets forth the alleged violation and which shall inform the alleged violator of his right to be heard on the accusation. 
(b)  Hearings. If a person accused of violating this article so requests, a hearing shall be scheduled, the time and place of which shall be published and provided to the accused violator. 
(c)  Decision. If the city determines that a violation of this article did occur, that decision, along with the hearing officer's reasons for finding a violation and the penalty to be imposed under section 12-272, shall be recorded in writing, a copy of which shall be provided to the accused violator. Likewise, if the hearing officer finds that no violation occurred or finds grounds for not imposing any penalty, such findings shall be recorded and a copy provided to the acquitted accused violator. 
(d)  Appeals. Appeals of any decision made by the hearing officer shall be filed in the district court for the city in which the alleged violation occurred. 
(e)  Misdemeanor prosecution. Nothing in this section shall prohibit the city from seeking prosecution as a misdemeanor for any alleged violation of this article. If the city elects to seek misdemeanor prosecution, no administrative penalty shall be imposed. 
(f)  Continued violation. Each violation, and every day in which a violation occurs or continues, shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 12; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-274. - Responsibility. 
    All licensees under this article shall be responsible for the actions of their employees in regard to the sale of tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices on the licensed premises, and the sale of such an item by an employee shall be considered a sale by the license holder. Nothing in this section shall be construed as prohibiting the city from also subjecting the employee to whatever penalties are appropriate under this article, state or federal law, or other applicable law or regulation. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 9; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-275. - Compliance checks and inspections. 
    All licensed premises shall be open to inspection by the city police or other authorized city official during regular business hours. From time to time, but at least once per year, the city shall conduct compliance checks by engaging, with the written consent of their parents or guardians, minors over the age of 15 years but less than 18 years, to enter the licensed premises to attempt to purchase tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices. Minors used for the purpose of compliance checks shall be supervised by city-designated law enforcement officers or other designated city personnel. Minors used for compliance checks shall not be guilty of unlawful possession of tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices when such items are obtained as a part of the compliance check. No minor used in compliance checks shall attempt to use a false identification misrepresenting the minor's age, and all minors lawfully engaged in a compliance check shall answer all questions about the minor's age asked by the licensee or his employee and shall produce any identification, if any exists, for which he is asked. Nothing in this section shall prohibit compliance checks authorized by state or federal laws for educational, research, or training purposes, or required for the enforcement of a particular state or federal law. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 10; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-276. - Prohibited sales. 
    It shall be a violation of this article for any person to sell or offer to sell any tobacco, tobacco product, or tobacco-related device: 
(1)  To any person under the age of 18 years. 
(2)  By means of any type of vending machine, except as may otherwise be provided in this article. 
(3)  By means of self-service methods whereby the customer does not need to make a verbal or written request to an employee of the licensed premise in order to receive the tobacco, tobacco product, or tobacco-related device and whereby there is not a physical exchange of the tobacco, tobacco product, or tobacco-related device between the licensee, or the licensee's employee, and the customer. 
(4)  By means of loosies. 
(5)  Containing opium, morphine, jimsonweed, belladonna, strychnos, cocaine, marijuana, or other deleterious, hallucinogenic, toxic, or controlled substances except nicotine and other substances found naturally in tobacco or added as part of an otherwise lawful manufacturing process. 
(6)  By any other means, to any other person, or in any other manner or form prohibited by federal, state, or other local law, ordinance, provision, or other regulation. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subds. 6, 11(A); Ord. No. 97-06) 
State Law reference- Sale of tobacco or other nicotine delivery products to children, Minn. Stats. §§ 609.685, 609.6855. 
Sec. 12-277. - Vending machines. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person licensed under this article to allow the sale of tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices by the means of a vending machine unless minors are at all times prohibited from entering the licensed establishment. Any retailer selling tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices at the time the ordinance from which this article is derived is adopted shall comply with this section within 90 days. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 7; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-278. - Self-service merchandising. 
    It shall be unlawful for a licensee under this article to allow the sale of tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices by any means whereby the customer may have access to such items without having to request the item from the licensee or the licensee's employee and whereby there is not a physical exchange of the tobacco, tobacco product, or the tobacco-related device between the licensee or his employee and the customer. All tobacco, tobacco products, and tobacco-related devices shall either be stored behind a counter or other area not freely accessible to customers, or in a case or other storage unit not left open and accessible to the general public. Any retailer selling tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices at the time the ordinance from which is article is derived is adopted shall comply with this section within 90 days. This section shall not apply to retail stores which derive at least 90 percent of their revenue from tobacco and tobacco-related products and which cannot be entered at any time by persons younger than 18 years of age. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 8; Ord. No. 97-06) 
State Law reference- Ban on sale of self-service packs of tobacco, Minn. Stats. § 461.18. 
Sec. 12-279. - Illegal sales. 
    It shall be a violation of this article for any person to sell or otherwise provide any tobacco, tobacco product, or tobacco-related device to any minor. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 11(A); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Secs. 12-280-12-306. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal tobacco licenses, Minn. Stats. § 461.12, subd. 1. 

Sec. 12-307. - Required. 
    No person shall sell or offer to sell any tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related device without first having obtained a license to do so from the city. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-308. - Application and issuance. 
(a)  Application. An application for a license to sell tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices shall be made on a form provided by the city. The application shall contain the full name of the applicant, the applicant's residential and business addresses and telephone numbers, the name of the business for which the license is sought, and any additional information the city deems necessary. Upon receipt of a completed application, the city administrator shall forward the application to the city council for action at its next regularly scheduled council meeting. If the administrator shall determine that an application is incomplete, he shall return the application to the applicant with notice of the information necessary to make the application complete. 
(b)  Action. The city council may either approve or deny the license, or it may delay action for such reasonable period of time as necessary to complete any investigation of the application or the applicant it deems necessary. If the city council approves the license, the administrator shall issue the license to the applicant. If the council denies the license, notice of the denial shall be given to the applicant along with notice of the applicant's right to appeal the council's decision. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3(A), (B); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-309. - Moveable place of business. 
    No license shall be issued to a moveable place of business. Only fixed location businesses shall be eligible to be licensed under this division. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3(F); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-310. - Basis for denial of license. 
    The following shall be grounds for denying the issuance or renewal of a license under this division; however, except as may otherwise be provided by law, the existence of any particular ground for denial does not mean that the city must deny the license. If a license is mistakenly issued or renewed to a person, it shall be revoked upon the discovery that the person was ineligible for the license under this section: 
(1)  The applicant is under the age of 18 years. 
(2)  The applicant has been convicted within the past five years of any violation of a federal, state, or local law, ordinance, provision, or other regulation relating to tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices. 
(3)  The applicant has had a license to sell tobacco, tobacco products, or tobacco-related devices revoked within the preceding 12 months of the date of application. 
(4)  The applicant fails to provide any information required on the application, or provides false or misleading information. 
(5)  The applicant is prohibited by federal, state, or local law, ordinance, or other regulation from holding such a license. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 5; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-311. - Fees. 
    No license shall be issued under this division until the appropriate license fee shall be paid in full. The fee schedule for a license under this division shall be on file at city hall. Initial license applications for a period of less than one year shall be charged a fee on a pro rata basis. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 4; Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-312. - Term. 
    All licenses issued under this division shall expire on February 1 of each year. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3(C); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-313. - Renewals. 
    The renewal of a license issued under this division shall be handled in the same manner as the original application. The request for a renewal shall be made at least 30 days but no more than 60 days before the expiration of the current license. The issuance of a license issued under this division shall be considered a privilege and not an absolute right of the applicant and shall not entitle the holder to an automatic renewal of the license. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3(H); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-314. - Transfers. 
    All licenses issued under this division shall be valid only on the premises for which the license was issued and only for the person to whom the license was issued. No transfer of any license to another location or person shall be valid without the prior approval of the city council. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3(E); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-315. - Display. 
    All licenses shall be posted and displayed in plain view of the general public on the licensed premises. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3(G); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Sec. 12-316. - Revocation or suspension. 
    Any license issued under this division may be revoked or suspended as provided in sections 12-272 and 12-273. 
(Prior Code, ch. 406, subd. 3(D); Ord. No. 97-06) 
Chapter 14 - NUISANCES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to define, prevent and abate nuisances, Minn. Stats. § 412.221, subd. 23. 

Sec. 14-1. - Abatement procedures. 
(a)  Applicable nuisances. This section shall apply to the abatement of public nuisances maintained exterior to the principal structure, including reported or observed junk as defined in section 101-3, outside storage of materials and equipment, including, but not limited to, tall grass and weeds as provided in chapter 8, article III, unused machinery, household appliances and furnishings, tires, excess vehicles, automotive parts, scrap metal, lumber, and the maintenance of any other materials, equipment or animals deemed to unreasonably annoy, injure, or endanger the safety, morals, comfort, or repose of any considerable number of people. 
(b)  Inspections. The city shall cause to be inspected all public and private properties within the city which may contain an exterior public nuisance. Such inspections shall take place as often as practicable to determine whether any such conditions exist. The city shall also investigate all reports of exterior public nuisances located within the city. 
(c)  Presence of nuisance; order for abatement. Whenever the city finds that an exterior public nuisance exists on any public or private property in the city, the city shall notify the affected property owner by first class mail that the nuisance must be abated within a reasonable period of time. Service by mail shall be deemed complete upon mailing. The order for abatement shall set forth the following: 
(1)  The specific nature of the violations and requirements for compliance. 
(2)  The date of the meeting and that the owner may appear. 
(3)  That failure to abate the nuisance within the applicable time period may result in summary abatement procedures. 
(d)  Disposal of property. The city maintains the right to dispose of all property that it removes from public and private properties through abatement procedures as outlined in this section. Disposal of property deemed to have value shall occur 30 days after the property is secured, unless the property owner obtains a court order to the contrary and/or pays all costs associated with the removal and storage of said property within the 30-day time period. The city maintains the right to immediately dispose of refuse and/or junk materials deemed to be without value. 
(e)  Cost of abatement. The city shall determine the abatement procedure for each nuisance and prepare a report outlining the costs thereof, which shall include an additional administrative charge of 25 percent of the cost to abate or $150.00, whichever is greater, to cover any administrative costs associated with the abatements. On or before September 1 of each year, the enforcement officer shall list the total unpaid charges for each abatement against each separate lot or parcel to which they are attributable under this section, based on the charges accumulated by the city administrator or designee. 
(f)  Reclamation procedure. To reclaim those materials that have been removed as a part of the abatement process, the owner or lien holder must pay any costs and administration fees incurred by the city. The owner or lien holder reclaiming the materials shall sign a release of property and shall agree not to return the items to their original location in violation of this Code. If additional removal of the same or similar items is deemed necessary by the city, an abbreviated but reasonable notice period will be provided before the removal takes place. All other provisions of this section, including the right to a hearing, shall continue to apply. 
(g)  Non-exclusiveness. Nothing in this section shall be deemed a waiver or limitation of any statutory right and/or power of the city as to hazardous buildings, properties or materials, nor shall this section be deemed to otherwise limit the right and/or power of the city to conduct other administrative and/or regulatory searches and inspections, including, but not limited to, health inspections, fire scene and arson inspections and regulated business and industries inspections, nor shall this article be deemed to be an exclusive remedy of the city regarding the abatement of exterior public nuisances. 
(Prior Code, ch. 611, subd. 1) 
Sec. 14-2. - Public nuisances. 
    Whoever, by his act or failure to perform a legal duty, intentionally does any of the following, is guilty of maintaining a public nuisance and may be ordered to abate the nuisance as provided herein, charged with a misdemeanor, or both: 
(1)  Maintaining offensive conditions. Maintains or permits a condition that unreasonably annoys, injures, or endangers the safety, health, morals, comfort or repose of any considerable number of people, including, but not limited to, the maintenance of junk, materials, equipment or animals exterior to a principal structure in violation of this Code. 
(2)  Obstructing public ways and waterways. Interferes with, obstructs, or renders dangerous for passage any public highway or right-of-way or waters used by the public. 
(3)  Interfering with health officials. Willfully opposes or obstructs a health officer or physician charged with the enforcement of health laws in performing any legal duties. 
(4)  Depositing used tires. Deposits or allows depositing of used or waste tires upon public or private property that is not a tire recycling, processing or receiving site approved by the city. 
(5)  Permitting accumulation of debris. Maintains or permits the accumulation of discarded or unused machinery, household appliances, automobile bodies, lumber, wood, trash, debris, or other material, or the rank growth of vegetation among the items so accumulated. 
(6)  Maintaining junk motor vehicles. Parks, keeps, stores or accumulates junk motor vehicles upon any private land or premises owned, occupied or controlled by any person or legal entity unless authorized by this Code or other ordinance. No person shall park, keep or place any such junk vehicle upon land not owned by such person. For the purposes of this section, a junk vehicle means a motor vehicle, as defined in Minn. Stats. § 169.011, that: 
a.  Is extensively damaged, with the damage including such things as broken or missing wheels, motor, drive train, or transmission; or 
b.  Is apparently inoperable; or 
c.  Does not have a valid, current registration plate. 
(7)  Maintaining dilapidated structures. Maintains or permits the existence of any structure or part of any structure which, due to fire, wind, other natural disaster, physical deterioration, or any other cause, is no longer habitable as a dwelling or is no longer useful for any other purpose for which it may have been intended. 
(8)  Failing to maintain integrity of dwelling unit. Fails to keep all exterior elements of residential dwelling units in the city in a clean, sanitary and structurally safe condition and in sound repair, including: 
a.  Stairways, porches, balconies, or decks; 
b.  Windows and doors; 
c.  Soffit and fascia; 
d.  Roofs; 
e.  Siding, bricks, stone or stucco; and 
f.  All other exterior elements not specifically listed.
