(9)  Failing to conceal remodeling materials. Fails to keep all materials being used in remodeling projects in a neat and orderly appearance and out of view from adjoining property for the duration of the project. 
(10)  Failing to properly store refuse. Fails to keep garbage and refuse in proper storage containers (bins or dumpsters) and regularly disposed of, as set forth in section 14-3. 
(11)  Dumping in streets or rights-of-way. 
a.  Throws or deposits in a street or right-of-way nails, dirt, glass or glassware, cans, discarded cloth or clothing, metal scraps, garbage, leaves, grass or tree limbs, paper or paper products, shreds or rubbish, oil, grease or other petroleum products, or to empty water containing salt or other injurious chemicals thereon. City, county, and state road maintenance, snow plowing, and related activities are exempt from this subsection. 
b.  Hauls any such material as described in subsection (11)a of this section inadequately enclosed or covered, thereby permitting the same to fall upon streets. It is unlawful to place or store building materials or waste resulting from building construction or demolition on a street. 
(12)  Other conditions. Performs any other act or omission declared by state law or city ordinance to be a public nuisance. 
(Prior Code, ch. 601, subd. 2; Ord. No. 10-01; Ord. No. 10-04) 
Sec. 14-3. - Solid waste. 
(a)  Definitions. The definitions in section 12-244 apply to this section. 
(b)  Accumulation prohibited; disposal required. Every household, occupant, or owner of any residence, commercial or industrial establishment shall, in a sanitary manner, dispose of refuse and recyclables that may accumulate upon the owner's or occupant's property on a weekly basis through a collection service licensed by the city or by other methods approved by the city. Recyclables shall be collected, at a minimum, every two weeks. 
(c)  Refuse, recyclables and yard waste. 
(1)  Prohibited deposits. No person shall place any refuse, recyclables or yard waste in any street or public place, or upon any private property, except in proper containers for collection. No person shall throw or deposit refuse, recyclables or yard waste in any body of water or in such manner as to cause litter or contamination of the environment. 
(2)  Burying refuse. No person shall bury any refuse in the city except in an approved sanitary landfill. 
(d)  Composting. Composting shall be allowed only on properties where there is a single-family detached dwelling or property operated by the city as an essential service. Composting is permitted on private property if all of the following conditions are met: 
(1)  Permitted material. Only organic materials, yard waste and easily biodegradable, nonpoisonous garbage may be composted. 
(2)  Dimensions of compost area. Composting shall be placed in a container or pile not to exceed 50 square feet in area or three feet in height. 
(3)  Location. The compost piles or containers shall be located in the rear yard at least five feet from any property line or 20 feet from a side lot line, if adjacent to any public street right-of-way. If a rear yard location is unavailable or impractical, the compost materials may be placed in another location approved by the city administrator or his authorized designee. 
(4)  Screening required. All compost piles and containers shall be fully screened so as not to be visible from adjacent properties and public rights-of-way as viewed from ground level. 
(5)  Maintenance required. Compost containers and compost materials shall be maintained so as not to create odors, rodent harborage, fire hazards or other nuisances. 
(Prior Code, ch. 607, subds. 3-5) 
State Law reference- Unlawful deposit of garbage, litter, etc., Minn. Stats. § 609.08. 
Sec. 14-4. - Hazardous buildings or hazardous property; definition. 
    The provisions of this section apply to a hazardous building or hazardous property as defined in Minn. Stats. § 463.15 and such definition is hereby adopted by reference. 
(Prior Code, ch. 914, subd. 1; Ord. No. 08-07) 
Sec. 14-5. - Notice to owner. 
    The building official shall examine or cause to be examined every property, building or structure or portion thereof which is dangerous or damaged and, if such is found to be a hazardous building or hazardous property, the building official shall give to the owner thereof written notice stating the defects therein, and shall indicate the improvements or repairs to be made, and may state that if repairs and improvements are impractical and not feasible to ultimately provide for the public safety and health, that such building or structure shall be removed. All such work shall be started and completed within a reasonable period of time as so stipulated in the notice by the building official. Such notice may require the property, building, structure, or portion thereof to be vacated forthwith and not reoccupied until the required repairs and improvements are completed, inspected, and approved by the building official. Proper service of such notice shall be by personal service upon the owner and lien holders of record or by publication for four weeks in the legal newspaper and concurrent posting on the property. If, in the event of an emergency situation, the building official determines that, to protect the public interests of health and safety, precautions and/or repairs or removal must be conducted immediately, the building official shall order the immediate cordoning off of any or all areas surrounding such property, building or structure causing the emergency conditions, and the building official shall notify the owner of record forthwith and order repairs to be commenced immediately. In the event notice cannot be made effective in sufficient time for the owner to abate the condition or properly cordon off the area, the city shall order necessary precautions to protect the public, and notice of such actions shall be made to the owner of record forthwith. 
(Prior Code, ch. 914, subd. 2; Ord. No. 08-07) 
Sec. 14-6. - Posting of signs. 
(a)  The building official shall cause to be posted at each entrance to such property or building a notice to read: 
DO NOT ENTER 
UNSAFE TO OCCUPY 
PUBLIC WORKS/BUILDING DEPARTMENT 
CITY OF OAK GROVE  
(b)  Such notice shall remain posted until the required repairs, demolition, or removal is completed. Such notice shall not be removed without written permission of the building official and no person shall enter the building except for the purpose of making the required repairs or for demolishing the building. 
(Prior Code, ch. 914, subd. 4; Ord. No. 08-07) 
Sec. 14-7. - Right to demolish. 
    In case the owner shall fail, neglect, or refuse to comply with the notice to repair, rehabilitate, or to demolish and remove said property, building or structure or portion thereof, the city may order the owner thereof prosecuted as a violator of the provisions of this article and may order the building official to proceed with the work specified in such notice. A statement of the cost of such work shall be transmitted to the council, who shall cause the same to be paid and levied as a special assessment against the property. 
(Prior Code, ch. 914, subd. 5; Ord. No. 08-07) 
Sec. 14-8. - Costs. 
    Costs incurred under provisions of this article shall be paid out of the city general fund. The city administrator or designee shall keep an accurate account of the expenses incurred in carrying out the order and of all other expenses theretofore incurred in connection with its enforcement. Such costs shall be charged to the owner of the premises involved as a special assessment on the land on which the building or structure is located, and shall be collected in the manner provided for special assessments, but the assessment shall be certified for collection as other special assessments. 
(Prior Code, ch. 914, subd. 6; Ord. No. 08-07) 
Sec. 14-9. - Prohibition. 
    It is unlawful for the owner of any property to suffer or permit a hazardous building or hazardous property to exist. 
(Prior Code, ch. 914, subd. 7; Ord. No. 08-07) 
State Law reference- Hazardous and substandard buildings, Minn. Stats. § 463.15 et seq. 
Chapter 16 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS 

Sec. 16-1. - Interference with city officers and employees. 
    No person shall prevent, delay or interfere with any city officer or employee engaged in the performance of his official duties. 
(Prior Code, ch. 601, subd. 4; Ord. No. 10-01) 
Sec. 16-2. - Noise. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Noise means any sound that is unwanted, does not occur in the natural environment, or has an erratic, intermittent, or statistically random oscillation. 
(b)  Loud, disturbing or excessive noise unlawful. It shall be unlawful for any person to make, continue, permit, or cause to be made or continued within the city any loud, disturbing or excessive noise which would be likely to cause significant discomfort or annoyance to a reasonable person of normal sensitivities present in the area. 
(c)  Characteristics; conditions. The characteristics and conditions which shall be considered in determining whether a noise is loud, disturbing or excessive for the purposes of subsection (b) of this section shall include, but not be limited to, the following: 
(1)  The land use, nature, and zoning of the area from which the noise emanates and the area where it is received. 
(2)  The time of day or night when the noise occurs. 
(3)  The duration of the noise. 
(4)  Whether the noise is recurrent, intermittent, or constant. 
(5)  Whether or not noise abatement measures are possible and whether or not they are used to reduce the sound level. 
(6)  The number of people and their activities that are affected by the noise. 
(7)  The volume and intensity of the noise. 
(Prior Code, ch. 603, subds. 2, 3) 
State Law reference- Authority to regulate and prevention noise, Minn. Stats. § 412.221, subd. 24. 
Sec. 16-3. - On-street parking. 
(a)  Manner of parking. Every vehicle parked upon any street with a curb shall be parked parallel thereto and with the right hand wheels within 12 inches of the curb. On streets without curbs, motor vehicles shall be parked only to the right of the traveled portion of the roadway and parallel thereto and in such a manner so as not to interfere with the flow of traffic. 
(b)  No-parking areas. No person shall stop, stand, or park a vehicle, except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance with the directions of a police officer or other traffic control device, in any of the following places: 
(1)  On a sidewalk. 
(2)  So as to block a public or private driveway. 
(3)  Within an intersection. 
(4)  Within ten feet of a fire hydrant. 
(5)  So as to block a crosswalk. 
(6)  At any place where official signs prohibit parking. 
(7)  Upon the shoulders of any trunk highway within the city. 
(8)  Upon any city road or street for a period of 24 continuous hours or more. 
(9)  Upon any city road or street after there has been an accumulation of one inch or more of snowfall until such time as the snow has been plowed from the road or street. 
(10)  Upon any city road or street in residential areas when such vehicle is a semi-truck, trailer, recreational vehicle or commercial vehicle, except when such vehicle is parked for the purposes of contracted work, and only then from dawn to dusk. 
(c)  Additional parking restrictions. Notwithstanding the foregoing restrictions, the city council may impose additional parking restrictions on roads and streets within the city if, in its opinion, such restrictions are necessary to protect the health, safety and welfare of persons or property. Roads and streets subject to such additional restrictions shall be designated by city council resolution, and such restrictions shall not be enforced until posted notice thereof on such roads or streets has taken place. 
(Prior Code, ch. 906, subd. 1; Ord. No. 08-14; Ord. No. 09-07; Ord. No. 12-02, 4-30-2012) 
Sec. 16-4. - Vehicle towing; violations. 
(a)  Removal, towing of vehicles. 
(1)  The designated law enforcement official is hereby authorized and empowered to remove or cause to be removed any vehicle parked, stored, stalled, or standing on city roads or streets in violation of any of the provisions of this section. 
(2)  Such vehicle may be removed by towing or otherwise and stored for safekeeping. Said vehicles shall not be removed from the places where they are stored until the owners or authorized agents shall have fully paid the costs incurred for towing and storage to the person or firm who has furnished such service. 
(3)  In the event that any vehicle held or stored is not claimed or recovered by the owner thereof, there is deemed to be imposed upon such vehicle a possessory lien for the amount of the costs incurred for towing and storage. Such lien shall be foreclosed in the manner provided by law for the foreclosure of possessory liens. 
(b)  Violations. 
(1)  Upon proof that a certain vehicle was parked, stored, or allowed to stand in violation of this section and that a certain person is the registered owner of said vehicle, this shall be prima facie evidence that such person committed or authorized the commission of such violation. 
(2)  At the direction of the designated law enforcement official, a citation may be issued in connection with any motor vehicle parked in violation of this section. 
(3)  Any person, firm, or corporation violating any provision of this section shall be guilty of a petty misdemeanor. 
(Prior Code, ch. 906, subds. 1, 2; Ord. No. 12-02, 4-30-2012) 
State Law reference- Stopping, standing and parking, Minn. Stats. § 169.32; authority to regulate standing or parking of vehicles, Minn. Stats. § 169.04(a)(1). 
Sec. 16-5. - Firearms. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Firearm means a gun that discharges shot or a projectile by means of an explosive or a gas. For the purposes of this section, a gun that discharges a shot or projectile by compressed air is not considered a firearm. 
    Owner means a person having a right or interest in the subject property, evidence of which is filed and recorded in the office of the county recorder or registrar of titles. 
(b)  Prohibited use. Near buildings. No person shall use, fire or discharge a firearm in the city within 300 feet of any dwelling, house, or commercial or industrial building. A person, however, may use, fire or discharge a firearm within such distance of a dwelling, house, or commercial or industrial building which is owned by that person or if the person has the written consent of the owner of the property to so use, fire, or discharge a firearm. 
(c)  Permitted discharges; restrictions. 
(1)  When discharging a firearm, the projectile shall not carry beyond the property line. 
(2)  All state game and fish and hunting laws or regulations must be complied with, but if there is any conflict between this article and state laws or regulations, the more restrictive shall apply, with the exception of hunting hours. 
(3)  Firearm discharges which are not prohibited herein and are not associated with legal hunting activities, are only permitted from one hour after sunrise to one hour prior to sunset. 
(d)  Exemptions. 
(1)  The provisions of this section shall not apply to the discharge of firearms, rifles or handguns when done in lawful defense of persons or property. No part of this section is intended to abridge the constitutional right to keep and bear arms. 
(2)  The city council may approve an exemption to this section, with reasonable conditions to protect public health, safety and welfare, to allow the discharge of firearms and bows for the following: 
a.  For the purpose of managing and controlling wildlife populations, provided the hunt has received support from the Minnesota Department of Natural Resources. 
b.  For target shooting as an accessory use to a retail business or as a special event or competition. 
c.  For law enforcement training purposes. 
(Ord. No. 15-05, § 1, 10-12-2015) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 15-05, § 1, adopted October 12, 2015, set out provisions intended for use as § 16-4. For purposes of clarity, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as § 16-5. 
Chapter 18 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- General authority relative to parks, Minn. Stats. § 412.221, subd. 6; parks generally, Minn. Stats. ch. 448. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 18-1-18-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PUBLIC CONDUCT IN PARKS AND RECREATIONAL AREAS 

Sec. 18-19. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Motor vehicle means any vehicle containing a unit for propelling it by means of converted, stored energy. 
    Park means any area owned by the city and designated by the city as a park area. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 1) 
Sec. 18-20. - Fireworks and explosives. 
    No fireworks or explosives shall be carried into or discharged in city parks except when approved by the city. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(A); Ord. No. 10-03) 
State Law reference- Fireworks, Minn. Stats. § 624.40 et seq. 
Sec. 18-21. - Disturbing the peace. 
    No person shall disturb the peace in a city park. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(D); Ord. No. 10-03) 
State Law reference- Disorderly conduct, Minn. Stats. § 609.32. 
Sec. 18-22. - Commercial activities. 
    No person shall engage in commercial activity of any kind within a city park except when expressly authorized by the city. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(E); Ord. No. 10-03) 
Sec. 18-23. - Animals. 
(a)  No person shall bring a dog or other domestic animal into a park unless the animal is kept leashed or under the direct control of its owner. The owner must pick up all feces of his dog or domestic animal. 
(b)  No person shall hunt, harm or remove any animal, reptile or bird within a city park without permission of the city. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(F), (H); Ord. No. 10-03) 
Sec. 18-24. - Vegetation. 
    No person shall cut or otherwise injure any flowers, shrubs, or trees in a city park. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(G); Ord. No. 10-03) 
State Law reference- Damage to property, Minn. Stats. § 609.595. 
Sec. 18-25. - Motor vehicles. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle within a city park except upon a designated roadway, and no person shall operate a motor vehicle within a city park at a speed in excess of 15 miles per hour. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(I); Ord. No. 10-03) 
Sec. 18-26. - Hours of operation. 
    No person shall occupy a city park between 11:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. unless authorized by the city. Any exceptions to these hours will be posted at the applicable park. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(J); Ord. No. 08-03; Ord. No. 10-03) 
Sec. 18-27. - Fires. 
    No person shall ignite a fire in a city park except in containers or in places where signs clearly designate that fires are permitted. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(K); Ord. No. 10-03) 
Sec. 18-28. - Posting signs or advertisements. 
    No person shall post any sign or advertisement in a city park unless authorized by the city. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(L); Ord. No. 10-03) 
Sec. 18-29. - Group permits. 
    Whenever any group, association or organization desires to use park facilities for a particular purpose, such as group picnics, group sporting activities, parties or theatrical, musical or other entertainment events, a representative of the group shall first obtain a group park permit from the city clerk for such use. The clerk shall require that the applicant pay for extra police protection or any special services if it appears that such protection is necessary. The clerk's decision to grant or deny an application for group park use may be appealed to the city council by the applicant or by any city resident by such person requesting placement of the issue on the agenda of the next regular city council meeting. 
(Prior Code, ch. 904, subd. 2(M); Ord. No. 10-03) 
Chapter 20 - SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS AND SPECIAL CHARGES 

Sec. 20-1. - Personal liability for city services; billing and collection. 
(a)  In this section, the term "city service" means any or all of the following when furnished by the city or its agents: 
(1)  Utility service. 
(2)  Nuisance abatement. 
(3)  Services enumerated in Minn. Stats. § 429.101. 
(4)  Charges due to the city for false alarms for fire or other emergency services. 
(5)  Any governmental service for which the city is authorized to impose a service charge. 
(b)  Except as otherwise provided by law, the owner of property on which any city service has been performed is personally liable for the cost of the service; provided, however, that if a service is performed at the request of a tenant of the property or if a nuisance is abated that was created by the tenant of the property, the tenant shall also be liable for the cost of the city service. Upon completion or delivery of a service under this section, the city administrator or other designated official shall prepare and mail an invoice to the owner and thereupon such amount will be due and payable to the city. 
(c)  The city administrator or designee shall maintain records of city services performed. 
(d)  The city administrator shall cause a bill to be sent to the appropriate party and/or insurance carrier (if applicable), and therefore shall take such reasonable steps as may be necessary for the collection of all charges for a city service. 
(e)  If a charge for a city service remains unpaid 30 days after a notice of delinquency is sent to the recipient of the service, the city may collect the debt through any lawful means that a private party may use to collect an unsecured delinquent debt. Accordingly, a party shall be given 30 days from the date that an invoice for charges is sent to make payment with the city. Should the party fail to make payment within the time allowed, a notice of delinquency shall be sent to the party. Should the party fail to make payment within 30 days of sending a delinquency notice, the city shall employ whatever means available to it to collect the debt. The system for collection of any delinquent charges shall be based upon the principal place of residence or other property ownership of the party for whom the services of the fire department are rendered. 
(f)  The city is authorized to certify unpaid charges for a city service to the property taxes of delinquent recipients who own taxable real property. At the end of each year, the city administrator shall be charged with processing delinquent charges for collection with the property taxes if the party is a resident of the city. 
(g)  In recognition of the fact that other local units of government under contract with the fire department have the authority to collect debts through certification to property taxes for their residents, the city administrator shall make reasonable effort to ensure that other local units are using such authority to collect delinquent charges on the fire department's behalf. Delinquent bills for residents outside of the immediate service territory of the fire department shall be referred to a private collection firm once it has been determined that the city is not likely to collect the debt using its own devices. 
(h)  The charges imposed may be appealed to the city council by submitting the grounds for the appeal in writing to the city administrator, provided that the written request for appeal is received by the city administrator within 30 days after the initial invoice was sent by the city. The party may address the city council to discuss the appeal only upon consent of the council. The city council's findings shall be final. 
(Prior Code, ch. 122, subds. 4, 6; Prior Code, ch. 124, subds. 2, 4; Ord. No. 08-15) 
State Law reference- Collection of unpaid charges, Minn. Stats. §§ 366.011, 366.012, 415.01, 429.101 
Sec. 20-2. - Deferral of special assessments based upon hardship. 
(a)  The city council is authorized to approve the deferral of the payment of a special assessment against a homestead property in accordance with Minn. Stats. §§ 435.193-435.195. 
(b)  In order to be eligible for the deferral, the additional following conditions shall also be met: 
(1)  The annual adjusted gross income of the owner of the property shall not exceed the extremely low (30 percent) income limits guidelines as provided for the Anoka County Metropolitan Statistical Area (MSA); 
(2)  This deferral will not be granted in the event there is any other deferment on the property. 
(c)  The deferral shall exist only as long as the property owner qualifies for the deferral. 
(d)  Interest on the deferred special assessment may accrue during the deferral at the net interest rate of the improvement bond issue, as stated in the official bond document, per annum. The city council may require current payment of interest as a condition of deferral. The city council may defer interest for the same period as deferral of the special assessment upon adoption of a resolution finding the necessity for such deferral of interest. Accumulated interest and the deferred payments may be due and payable upon the occurrence of any of the following events: 
(1)  The death of the owner, provided that the spouse is not eligible for the benefits hereunder; 
(2)  The sale, transfer or subdivision of the property or any part thereof; 
(3)  If the property should for any reason lose its homestead status; or 
(4)  If for any reason, upon completion of due process, the city council determines that there would be no hardship to require immediate or partial payment. 
(e)  The deferral of payment of special assessments may be ordered by resolution of the city council at the request of the property owner at any time following adoption of the assessment role. The city administrator shall be responsible for preparing application forms to be completed by the property owner. The property owner shall immediately notify the city clerk's office of the existence of any change in status which may affect eligibility for deferral. 
(Prior Code, ch. 908, subd. 2; Ord. No. 09-09) 
Chapter 22 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- General authority relative to streets, Minn. Stats. § 412.221, subd. 6; acquisition of property for streets, Minn. Stats. ch. 440. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 22-1. - Construction of streets and roads. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    City engineer means the duly appointed engineering representative of the city. 
    Subdivider means any person commencing proceedings under chapter 107 to effect a subdivision of land owned by such subdivider or owned by another, as defined in said chapter, or splitting land through any other means. 
(b)  Scope. 
(1)  The rules and regulations governing the construction of streets and roads contained herein shall apply within the city and other land as permitted by state statutes. In the event of overlapping jurisdiction within the prescribed area, the extent of jurisdiction shall be determined and agreed upon between this city and the other municipality or municipalities concerned. 
(2)  It is not intended by this chapter to repeal, abrogate, annul or in any way impair or interfere with private agreements which are equal to or more restrictive, or with restrictive covenants running with land to which the city is a party, except that the most restrictive shall apply. 
(c)  Compliance. 
(1)  The development of new streets or upgrading of existing roads shall be either a public improvement or a private development. 
(2)  Public improvements shall follow the procedural requirements of Minn. Stats. ch. 429. These projects shall comply with the technical requirements of this chapter. 
(3)  Private developments shall follow the procedural requirements and technical requirements of this chapter. 
(d)  Preliminary plan. 
(1)  On-site ponding. Soil Conservation Service Technical Report #20 or equal shall be used as a basis of design for all on-site pond sizing. Refer to section 107-177. 
(2)  Soil tests. Soil testing shall only be required at city engineer's request. 
(3)  Pavement design calculations. A soils report shall be submitted by a registered professional soils engineer outlining the recommendations for the pavement design which in no event shall be less than the standards set forth in section 107-176 upon the city engineer's request. 
(4)  Horizontal and vertical alignment and grade calculations. The city shall forward the subdivider's submittals to its engineer for review. These documents shall be submitted to the city by the developer. 
(5)  Road design plan. Road design plan submittals shall include a typical pavement section, plan and profile sheets, and grading cross sections for every 100 feet of road. 
(6)  Proposed signs. Proposed signs shall be shown on the road design plans for review and approval by the engineer and public works supervisor or his designee. 
(e)  Approval of the preliminary plan, project plans and specifications of new streets or upgrade of existing roads. Prior to initiating any construction activities identified in the plans and specifications for construction, the subdivider shall accompany the public works supervisor or his designee and engineer on a site visit to review the proposed construction. Special consideration shall be given when roads are stubbed for future connection as required by section 107-148. 
(Prior Code, ch. 902, subds. 2-4) 
Sec. 22-2. - Boulevard encroachments. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Boulevard means the portion of the street right-of-way between the outside edge of the roadway and the property line. 
    Encroachment means any object, live or inanimate, situated within a public right-of-way, including, but not limited to, posts, trees, bushes, rocks, utility poles and boxes, retaining walls, etc. 
    Imminent danger means the likelihood of damage to a vehicle or injury to a pedestrian upon contact with the encroachment. 
    Impede means interference with pedestrian traffic to an unreasonable degree. 
(b)  Permit. Any person who intends to place an encroachment as defined herein within the public right-of-way shall obtain a permit prior thereto from the city engineer unless such encroachment is excepted pursuant to subsection (c) of this section. No permit shall be granted for encroachments which would be considered nuisances as defined in subsection (d) of this section. 
(c)  Exceptions. The terms and provisions of this section shall not apply to the following: 
(1)  Mailbox or newspaper delivery box stands meeting city standards. 
(2)  Traffic and directional signs. 
(3)  Utility poles and utility structures. 
(4)  Fire hydrants. 
(5)  Bus shelters or public benches. 
(d)  Nuisances. Any encroachment located within a public right-of-way that impedes pedestrian traffic or constitutes imminent danger to vehicular or pedestrian traffic on any boulevard constitutes a public nuisance. 
(e)  Maintenance of boulevard. Except as may be prohibited by this section or other provisions of this Code, the owner or occupant of property abutting a public right-of-way shall be responsible for the maintenance of the boulevard area adjacent to his property. The owner or occupant shall, at a minimum, maintain the lawn and trees in the boulevard. The city shall not be responsible for the maintenance of or liable for injury to or from such improvements, and the property owner or occupant agrees to hold the city harmless from any claims arising out of any injury or damage to or from such improvements. 
(Prior Code, ch. 910, subds. 2-5, 7) 
Secs. 22-3-22-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - RIGHT-OF-WAY MANAGEMENT[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Right-of-way management, Minn. Stats. §§ 237.162, 237.163. 

Sec. 22-23. - Definitions. 
    The definitions in Minn. Rules 7819.0100, subpts. 1-23 are hereby adopted by reference and are incorporated in this article as if set out in full. 
Sec. 22-24. - Election to manage the public right-of-way. 
    In accordance with Minn. Stats. § 237.163 subd. 2(b), the city hereby elects to manage rights-of-way within its jurisdiction. 
Sec. 22-25. - Permit requirement. 
(a)  Permit required. Except as otherwise provided herein, no person may obstruct or perform work in any right-of-way without first having obtained a permit from the city. The permit shall specify the location of the affected right-of-way, describe the work to be performed and facilities to be installed, and the duration of the permit. 
(b)  Permit extensions. No person may obstruct or perform work in the right-of-way beyond the date specified in a permit unless a new permit or permit extension is granted. 
(c)  Delay penalty. In accordance with Minn. Rules 7819.1000, subpt. 3, the city may impose a delay penalty for unreasonable delays in work conducted in the right-of-way. The city council may establish the amount of the delay penalty from time to time by resolution. 
(d)  Permit display. Permits issued under this article shall be conspicuously displayed or otherwise available at all times at the indicated work site for inspection. 
Sec. 22-26. - Permit applications. 
    A permit application shall contain the following: 
(1)  A completed application form, including all required plans or drawings showing the location and area of the proposed project and the location of all known existing and proposed facilities, and the following: 
a.  The applicant's name, gopher one-call registration certificate number, address and e-mail address, if applicable, and telephone and facsimile numbers. 
b.  A certificate of insurance naming the city as an additional insured, verifying that the applicant is insured against claims for personal injury, death, or property damages associated with work in the right-of-way, and requiring 30 days' notice to the city of cancellation or material modification of the policy. 
c.  If the applicant is a corporation, a copy of the certificate required to be filed under Minn. Stats. § 300.06 as recorded and certified to by the secretary of state. 
d.  A copy of the applicant's certificate of authority from the state public utilities commission, or other applicable state or federal agency, to the extent such authority is required by law. 
(2)  Payment of a permit fee covering the city's administrative and management costs and any associated costs, such as the cost of any right-of-way restoration that the city will complete. 
State Law reference- Gopher one-call registration, Minn. Stats. ch. 216D. 
Sec. 22-27. - Permit denial and conditions. 
(a)  The city may deny a permit if a completed application is not filed, if the requirements and conditions of this article are not met, or if the city determines that the denial is necessary to protect the health, safety, and welfare or to protect the right-of-way and its current use. 
(b)  The city may impose reasonable conditions upon the issuance of the permit to protect the health, safety and welfare or to protect the right-of-way and its current use. 
Sec. 22-28. - Permit fees. 
    The city shall establish an appropriate permit fee schedule which will be available to the public. Unless otherwise agreed to in a franchise, right-of-way permit fees are separate from and in addition to franchise fees imposed on a right-of-way user. Permit fees shall be set in an amount intended to recover the city's right-of-way management costs, including, but not limited to, costs of issuing, processing, and verifying permit applications; inspecting job sites and restoration projects; maintaining, supporting, protecting, or moving user facilities during right-of-way work, determining the adequacy of restoration work or restoring right-of-way to its original condition; and enforcing permits. Such costs do not include payment by a telecommunications right-of-way user for the use of the public right-of-way. 
Sec. 22-29. - Work standards. 
    All work performed in the right-of-way shall be done in conformance with Minn. Rules, pt. 7819.1100, or applicable local requirements. 
Sec. 22-30. - Right-of-way restoration by permittee. 
    Unless otherwise provided in a permit, the permittee shall promptly patch and restore the right-of-way to a condition equivalent to that prior to its work. The permittee shall complete restoration according to Minn. Rules, pt. 7819.1100, or such other standards as may be specified by the city. If the pavement settles, the permittee shall pay to the city all costs associated with correcting the problem within 30 days of billing. Upon the city's request, the permittee shall post a construction performance bond in accordance with the provisions of Minn. Rules, pt. 7819.3000. If the permittee fails to restore the right-of-way as required, the city may exercise its rights under the construction performance bond. 
Sec. 22-31. - Right-of-way restoration by city. 
    The city may choose to restore the right-of-way itself. If the city restores the right-of-way, the permittee shall pay the estimated costs thereof as part of the permit application fee. 
Sec. 22-32. - Inspection. 
(a)  Notice of completion. The permittee shall notify the city in writing when the work under a permit is completed. 
(b)  Site inspection. City personnel and others authorized by law may inspect the work site at any time during or upon completion of the work. At any time, the city may order cessation of work that poses a serious threat to the life, health, safety or well-being of the public. 
Sec. 22-33. - Work done without a permit. 
(a)  Non-emergencies. Except in an emergency, any person who obstructs or performs work in a right-of-way without the necessary permit must immediately obtain a permit and pay double the normal permit fee as a penalty. 
(b)  Emergency situations. Any person with facilities in the right-of-way shall immediately notify the city of any emergency in relation to its facilities. Such person may take whatever actions are necessary to respond to the emergency. Such person shall apply for the necessary permits, pay the fees associated therewith and fulfill the rest of the requirements of this article as soon as is feasible. 
Sec. 22-34. - Revocation of permit. 
    The city may revoke any right-of-way permit, without a fee refund, if there is a breach of the terms and conditions of any statute, ordinance, rule or regulation, or any material condition of the permit. Prior to revocation, the city shall make a written demand upon the permittee to remedy such violation. Within 24 hours of receipt, the permittee shall provide a plan acceptable to the city to cure the violation or breach. The permittee's failure to timely respond or implement the approved plan shall be cause for immediate revocation of the permit. If a permit is revoked, the city may make a demand in writing that the permittee remove his facilities from the right-of-way. If the permittee fails to complete removal within ten days of such demand, the city may remove the facilities and demand reimbursement from the permittee for such removal costs. In addition to any removal or restoration costs, the permittee shall reimburse the city for all other costs incurred by him in connection with the permit revocation, including, but not limited to, attorneys' fees. 
Sec. 22-35. - Mapping data. 
    Each permittee shall provide mapping information required by the city in accordance with Minn. Rules, pts. 7819.4000 and 7819.4100. 
Sec. 22-36. - Location of facilities. 
(a)  Undergrounding. Unless otherwise expressly permitted by law, new construction, installation of facilities, or the replacement of old facilities shall be done underground or contained within buildings or other structures in conformity with applicable law. Existing above-ground facilities may be repaired in place. 
(b)  Additional requirements. The city may impose restrictions on the location, size, design and appearance of any equipment or facilities to be located in the right-of-way. The city may assign specific corridors or locations within the right-of-way for each type of facility. Permits issued by the city may designate the proper corridor or location for the facilities at issue. The city may prohibit the placement of additional facilities within the right-of-way if necessary to protect health, safety, and welfare, or protect the right-of-way and its current use. 
Sec. 22-37. - Relocation of facilities. 
    Upon the city's written request, a person with facilities in the right-of-way shall promptly and at his own expense permanently remove and relocate his facilities as necessary to prevent interference in connection with a public project such as ditching or road improvements, or as the city may deem necessary to further public health or safety. 
Sec. 22-38. - Right-of-way vacation. 
    If the city vacates a right-of-way that contains the facilities of a permittee, the permittee's rights in the vacated right-of-way are governed by Minn. Rules, pt. 7819.3200. 
Sec. 22-39. - Indemnification and liability. 
    By applying for and accepting a permit, a permittee agrees to defend and indemnify the city in accordance with the provisions of Minn. Rules, pt. 7819.1250. 
Sec. 22-40. - Abandoned facilities. 
    Any person who has abandoned facilities in any right-of-way shall remove them from that right-of-way if necessary to accommodate other right-of-way repair, excavation, or construction. 
Sec. 22-41. - Appeal. 
    A right-of-way user that has been denied a permit, has had permit revoked, or believes that the fees imposed are invalid may have the denial, revocation, or fee imposition reviewed upon written request by the city council at its next regular meeting. A decision affirming the denial, revocation, or fee imposition will be in writing and supported by written findings establishing the reasonableness of the decision. 
Sec. 22-42. - Reservation of regulatory and police powers. 
    A permittee's rights are subject to the regulatory and police powers of the city to adopt and enforce general ordinances necessary to protect the health, safety and welfare of the public. 
Secs. 22-43-22-62. - Reserved. 
Sec. 22-63. - All terrain vehicles. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    All terrain vehicle or vehicle means a motorized flotation-tired vehicle of not less than three low pressure tires, but not more than six tires, that is limited in engine displacement of less than 1,000 cubic centimeters and total dry weight less than 1,000 pounds. 
    Golf cart means a passenger conveyance, electric or gasoline motor powered vehicle, with three or four low pressure tires and engine displacement not exceeding 800 cubic centimeters and a total dry weight not exceeding 800 pounds. 
(b)  Jurisdiction. This ordinance shall regulate the operation of all-terrain vehicles and golf carts on public roads under the jurisdiction of the city and on the streets and highways within the boundaries of the city. 
(c)  Operation; youthful operators. No person shall operate an all-terrain vehicle or golf cart on public roadways in the city unless such person has in immediate possession a driver's license valid under Minnesota Statutes. 
(d)  State and county highways. No person shall operate an all-terrain vehicle or golf cart on the roadway, on the shoulder, or on the inside bank or slope of any trunk, county state-aid, or county highway in the city. 
(e)  City streets. All-terrain vehicles and golf carts may be operated within city streets provided that they are operated on the far right-hand side of the roadway surface and in the same direction as the roadway traffic on the nearest lane of the roadway except for turning or crossing movements at intersections. 
(f)  Maximum speed. All-terrain vehicles or golf carts in the city shall not exceed the legal speed limits of the road being traveled. 
(g)  Compliance with traffic laws. All-terrain vehicles and golf carts must be operated in compliance and conformity with all state, county, and local traffic laws, except those provisions which by their nature have no application. 
(h)  Private property. No person shall operate an all-terrain vehicle or golf cart on private property or upon lands not belonging to the operator of the vehicle without the written or oral permission of the landowner(s), or other person(s) entitled to the use and possession of such property. 
(i)  Operating under influence of alcohol or controlled substance. A person may not operate or be in control of an all-terrain vehicle or golf cart while under the influence of alcohol, as provided in Minn. Stats., § 169.121, subd. 1, or a mood altering drug, hallucinogen, or controlled substance defined in Minn. Stats., § 152.01, subd. 4. 
(j)  Registration number. No person shall operate an all-terrain vehicle without the registration number, assigned by the commissioner of natural resources, affixed to the vehicle in a plain and visible manner, as prescribed by the commissioner. 
(k)  Registration card. No person shall operate an all-terrain vehicle without having on his person the registration card provided by the commissioner of natural resources, which shall include the registration number, the date of registration, the make and serial number of the vehicle, the owner's name and address, and such additional information as the commissioner may require. 
(l)  Permit. The city may by resolution, issue a general permit to residents of the city to operate all-terrain vehicles and golf carts on city streets. 
(Ord. No. 13-08, § 1, 12-9-2013) 
Chapter 24 - UTILITIES[1]

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL
